It does not lather up well - this is to be expected, as it does not contain some of the arguable &#34;bad&#34; ingredients that cause a shampoo to foam. The work around, is to use a very small amount of the shampoo first through your hair and then rinse it out -- the second application will lather up exponentially better. You can also use a small amount of another shampoo for the first application to conserve your Regenepure supply.<br /><br />3. For me, it did not cure my &#34;itchy scalp&#34;; however, in my case the itchiness (and flakes) was caused primarily by morning/night applications ofLipogaine (Minoxidil). Switching to Rogaine foam in the morning, and Lipogaine liquid at night has all but stopped the itchiness and drastically reduced the amount of &#34;white flakes&#34;.<br /><br />4. Where I do believe it has helped hair growth, I would not recommend this product alone to fight hair loss -- I believe it is best used with 5% Minoxidil. On the flip side, I would also not recommend using Minoxidil alone, and would totally 100% recommend using this shampoo in addition.<br /><br />Side note:<br />I've used another brand of Ketoconazole shampoo (Lipogaine, the Big 3) as well; however, it left my hair feeling noticeably dry (it's to my understanding that Ketoconazole is drying, which is why the Aloe in Regenepure helps counter balance that effect).<br /><br />I would totally recommend that you, at least, give Regenepure a try - it's my favorite shampoo by far, and I hope they keep making the product for years to come.
  225. I've been using Regenepure DR by itself, almost daily, for just over a year now. I've also since then been using 5% minoxidil, and so it's hard to attribute all my hair growth/retention to Regenepure DR. However, this summer I took a break from the shampoo for a couple weeks, just to see what would happen, while maintaining my minoxidil applications, and noticed much more hair thinning toward the front of my head; the advanced thinning stopped when I continued its use. So, I'm rather sure that while Regenepure DR isn't too effective at growing hair back (as ketoconazole, its active ingredient, isn't known for doing), it is effective at retaining much of the hair you have (which ketoconazole is known for doing). I still have a relatively full head of hair, with some thinning present on the crown and some lightly emerging on the sides and front, and so couldn't attest to Regenepure DR's efficacy on more advanced stages of male pattern baldness. I also think it's pretty important to note that I've had all the success I've had with Regenepure DR not using Regenepure NT. Essentially, I think it's pretty expendable to your routine if you already use a good conditioner (I just use a cheap Suave humecant); the Regenepure DR will probably run you about a bottle a month, at around $30, and so it's good to cut corners like Regenepure NT whenever possible if on a budget. All in all, Regenepure DR is a great and revitalizing shampoo in general, and seems to be rather effective in slowing thinning. Although its price is a little steep, I would definitely recommend it.
